## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (deterministic rate-law ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics modeled by ordinary differential equations. With only A and t available, the most common relationships are empirical/mechanistic rate laws (order in A) and time-dependent effective rate constants (e.g., catalyst deactivation, changing conditions).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption/production: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate regime; surface/photochemical saturation, excess reactant)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; pseudo-first-order when another reactant is buffered)
- First-order with source term: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous feed or generation plus first-order loss; CSTR-like lumping)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear reversible limit): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order approximation)
- General nth-order power law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting; chain reactions/complex mechanisms lumped)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/limited capacity)
- Saturating/inhibited rate in A (rational form): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (self-inhibition, limited active sites, or empirical saturation in rate vs A)
- Higher-order polynomial rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order pathways)
- Time-dependent first-order (deactivating catalyst/aging): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant decreases with time)
- Time-dependent first-order (ramping conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant increases/decreases approximately linearly in time)
- Time-dependent power-law rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * (t + c1)**c2 * A (effective rate constant follows a power law in time; transport/aging effects)
- Oscillatory forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodically driven temperature/light/catalyst modulation, linearized as time-periodic k)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line when plotting dA_dt vs A at fixed t), it suggests first-order or pseudo-first-order kinetics: dA_dt ≈ -c * A.
- A nonzero intercept in dA_dt vs A (i.e., dA_dt ≈ c0 - c1*A) indicates an effective source/feed term or baseline generation competing with decay.
- Curvature consistent with dA_dt scaling like A**2 or A**n (log-log slope ~ n) suggests bimolecular or nth-order rate laws; mixed curvature often indicates sums like -c0*A - c1*A**2.
- A stable fixed point A* where dA_dt = 0 and the slope ∂(dA_dt)/∂A at A* is negative indicates relaxation-to-equilibrium behavior of the form -c*(A - A*).
- If |dA_dt| grows at low A but then diminishes as A increases (self-limiting), it points to autocatalytic-limited forms like c*A*(c1-A) or saturating rational forms A/(A+c).
- If the apparent rate constant inferred as (-dA_dt/A) changes systematically with t, it supports a time-dependent k(t) structure such as exp(-c*t), (t+c)**c, or (1+c*t).
- If dA_dt changes sign over time at similar A levels, it suggests external forcing or switching conditions, often captured by explicit t-dependence (e.g., sinusoidal or piecewise k(t)).
- If dynamics slow down strongly at long times independent of A level, it may indicate aging/transport limitation captured by k(t) decreasing with t (e.g., exp(-c*t) or (t+c)**(-p)).

### 1. \(A c0 e^{c1 t} + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)+c5\)

### 2. \(A c0 e^{c1 t} + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
Same as (1) but no constant term. Set \(c4=0\) and choose \(c0,c1,c2,c3\) as above. Works.

### 3. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A c3 + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\)

### 4. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + A^{c2} c3 e^{c4 t} + c5\sin(Ac6+c7)\)
